  32. It's easy to make jokes about Gillette's evolving product line: every few years the company adds another blade (or two) to their cartridge and changes the color of their razor handle. Jokes aside, however, each previous product (the Sensor Excel, the Mach 3, and the Fusion / Fusion Proglide) has marked a major leap forward in the shaving experience. Every time I've gone back and used a Mach 3, in fact, I've been struck by just how big a difference there is between that product and the far superior 5-blade Fusion (or its slightly-improved successor the Fusion Proglide). Given that experience, I was excited to try the Fusion Proglide with Flexball Handle (*full disclosure: the item was provided to me free from Gillette*), which features a hinge on the handle, supplementing the range of motion offered by the hinge on the cartridge itself (the hinge on the handle swivels left-to-right, while the hinge on the cartridge swivels forward-and-back). Unfortunately, the new handle did little to improve the shaving experience. Yes, the additional hinge does help keep the blades parallel to the shaver’s skin – but it doesn’t make nearly as great a difference as the hinge on the cartridge (which was one of the Mach 3’s novel features). The cartridge itself, meanwhile – which, after all, is the key to the shaving experience – remains basically unchanged. That’s not a problem: the Fusion Proglide cartridge is exceptional. But the value-add for the new handle is minimal. If you already have a Fusion / Fusion Proglide handle without the Flexball swivel, don’t bother buying this new product. That said, if you do *not* own a Fusion handle and you’re looking to buy one, the Flexball Handle does represent a marginal improvement on the old product.

I particularly liked that the blister pack that this razor comes in has a recycled pressed-paper backing. (Almost like cardboard, and easily recycled) The clear plastic front is still a wasteful land-filler, but at the very least, the packaging makes an attempt at being environmentally responsible. Also, packaged with the razor is a nice little plastic tray to set the razor on after your shave, keeping the head of the razor off the counter. Necessary? Probably not, but I kind of like it.<br /><br />The razor has a nice feel in your hand. It doesn't feel cheap or insubstantial. If you are at all familiar with previous Gillette Razors featuring the multi-blade head, this will not seem much different to you. The big difference here (or so Gillette would have you believe) is in the rotating head. As you shave, the razor's head swivels left and right, as well as up and down. The thinking is that this helps the razor maintain closer contact to you skin regardless of facial contours. It is a neat idea, but I found it a little difficult to get precise control over the razor because of the head's ability to swivel so easily. I really did not notice much difference in the quality of shave from this razor compared to earlier versions of the Gillette Fusion. It provides a close shave, leaving my skin smooth and irritation free.<br /><br />Since I got this razor for free and I haven't researched the price, I can't really speak to the cost of the handle, or the cost of replacement blade cartridges. I doubt they will be much different than earlier Fusions though, and that means a couple things. They will be a little on the spendy side ( I am a cheapskate, so we're talking in the neighborhood of ten to fifteen dollars for the razor itself, and nearly twenty bucks for a 4 count razor cartridge refill.) For me, a razor cartridge lasts a long time (6 to 9 months usually) because I don't shave daily. Typically I go four or five days between shaves, and I don't shave at all through the winter months, so keep that in mind and weigh it accordingly when considering my statement that a razor cartridge lasts a long time.<br /><br />As with previous fusion blades, the head will clog easily with stubble if not rinsed often. For me, since I don't shave daily, it goes something like stroke, followed by a rinse, stroke followed by a rinse, etc. etc. I use Gillette Shaving gel as well. Your choice in cream, gel, or other facial lubricant may have an impact on the razor's performance as well.<br /><br />In conclusion, I will say that the Gillette Fusion Proglide razor with \\"Flexball\\" technology provides a good, close shave. Is it the greatest thing since sliced bread? No, not really. Is it worth replacing whatever your using now? Again, no, probably not. But if you're in the market for a new razor anyway, you might as well give this one a shot as it does a good job.

  202. As with all manual, multiple blade shavers, I found I got a decent shave with this razor. I do tend to get a few ingrown hairs, which I can't necessarily fault the razor for, but this one was certainly no different in that respect. I had to pass over a few areas a few times; again, really nothing new. The &#34;Flexball&#34; handle was fine but more of a gimmick, IMO, than a really innovative technology. Plus there was a tiny bit of a learning curve to using it. My main gripes with this, or really any disposable razor these days, are 1) the lube strip works great for the 1st shave, just OK for the 2nd, and even if the blades are sharp enough for more shaves than that, the lube strips are useless; and 2) The refills are outrageously expensive. I am guessing that's why myself, and many others, got to try this for free from Gillette - they can make a mint back on us from buying refills for this. The truth is, I'm a simple guy and while I appreciate a close shave, and do think that multiple blades have improved shaving, the gimmicks (roller ball, vibration, lube strips, etc.) are really just ways to boost the cost of the refills without really changing the overall experience. Give me a few blades, some shaving cream, and I'm good to go. You probably won't hate this razor but you won't be blown away either.<br /><br />And just to be sure you understand, I did try this for free from Gillette.

  204. Here is my analysis and test results for the new Gillette &#34;Flexball&#34; razor:<br /><br />▲ The razor comes with a very handy stand to hold while not being used. Fits well, stays put. The razor is very hefty--about 1.8 oz measured on my scale. By contrast, a disposable typically weighs-in less than 1 oz. I measured a Gillette disposable at 1/2 oz.<br /><br />▲ The razor body is very solid, and has a comfortable feel to it. I liked the feel of the razor body--it felt solidly constructed, and is also well-balanced. I also liked the black raised ergonomic contours on the body of the razor. Again--felt very solid and well constructed. The color of the body is black with silver trim, plus the orange Flexball.<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #1,&#34; I did not shave for several days, so that I had a 3-day beard. I washed my face with cool water, left my face wet, then applied a smooth layer of the Proglide gel. I then waited several minutes for my beard to soften. I began shaving in the easier portions of my face, where the whiskers are lighter, then proceeded to the heavier sections around my chin. The razor nicely navigated all the crags and contours without the slightest drag or snagging. The blades cut very close without the hint of scraping or cutting. I examined my face very closely after shaving, and I was very pleased with the result. The razor did an outstanding job, providing a very close, clean shave. (For the records, I do NOT have a really smooth face--it's about normal roughness.)<br /><br />▲ For &#34;Field Test #2,&#34; I had just the normal 1-day beard. I washed my face with warm water, left my face wet, then similarly applied a layer of the same gel. I waited exactly 3 1/2 minutes for the bristles to soften. This time, I paid attention to how well the razor traversed over the chin and down to the neck. I wanted to see if the rotating head of the razor could smoothly navigate this hilly territory. As before the razor did a similarly outstanding job, providing a very close and smooth shave. Thus, both the Field Tests confirm the capability of this product. It works as advertised. When I completed my shaving, I rinsed the razor, and noticed that it is somewhat difficult to get the blades entirely clean of shaving gel. With 5 blades closely spaced together, this is not a trivial feat. After cleaning, I thoroughly dried the cartridge, as I hope to extend the life of the blades.<br /><br />▲ The famous &#34;Flexball&#34; is obvious because of its bright orange color. The Flexball pivots in 2 different ways. As you hold the razor in front of you, it pivots left to right, in an angular fashion--perhaps up to 15 degrees in each direction. There are little &#34;stops&#34; on the Flexball that prevent it from rotating too far. You can see a very fine band (at first I thought it was a wire) that allows the angular pivoting. This movement is very smooth--no hitches whatsoever. There is a small screw-like pivot-point, around which the movement takes place. This fastener appears to be very solid; I doubt anything will come lose. The head of the razor also pivots forward and back, using a thin &#34;bar&#34; going into the head of the razor.<br /><br />▲ The above Flexball is very impressive engineering. It appears to operate flawlessly. All of this is to allow the razor to match the contours of your face. That's a nice way of saying, shave around all those divots and dents in your face (not that YOU have any, of course, but someone else might.) To further get around those slight detours, this product uses extremely thin, five blades that are designed to glide more smoothly; thus, there is no tugging on your skin.<br /><br />▲ Gillette also claims to incorporate a proprietary strip called the &#34;Enhanced Lubrastrip.&#34; It's the part of the cartridge that is pale green. This strip contains mineral oil and &#34;lubricating polymers.&#34; Well, my skin appreciated those &#34;polymers.&#34;<br /><br />✔ SUMMARY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris LawsonY: My shaving &#34;test&#34; passed with flying colors. My shave was very smooth, very close, no tugs, no snags. The razor feels very solid. One possible caveat--the razor itself, and the replacement blades are not cheap compared to other products. However, it seems unfair to lower the rating because of the cost; the shopper can make their own decision.<br /><br />Highly Recommend!<br /><br />♫ A Review by Chris Lawson

  276. By far, the Fusion cartridge razors are probably some of the best. The problem is that for too long they have really just moderately changed the cartridges and considered it a major upgrade. So that is why I really took interest in the new FlexBall handle when I read about it. So when I saw a free trial of this razor from Gillette, I jumped on it.<br /><br />I think everyone has used a Fusion cartridge by now. It's real nice and does a great job getting close. I've used them on various handles and it really all seemed the same. This isn't the case with the FlexBall. One of the nice things about cartridge razors is they allow the blades to go up and down to keep contact with the face. The FlexBall also goes side to side. This allows the cartridge to stay in contact with the face better. This allows for an effortless close shave. Like most guys, I have problems with certain parts of my neck. With a couple of passes, those trouble areas are smoother than they've ever been. And the shave took probably half the time as normal.<br /><br />The handle itself is well built. It's mostly metal, which gives it a good heft, but it's not heavy. It have a very nice rubber padding to give it a good grip. The only, extremely minor, problem I had with it was trying out switching blades. Because the FlexBall end allows the head of the razor to rock side to side, the new cartridge may not line up and click in as easily as other handles in the Fusion line. But again it's extremely minor and with no real effort you can re-position and get it to click right in.<br /><br />Recently I switched to using a vintage Gillette Ball End Tech safety razor. I probably won't be switching from that, mainly for cost reasons. I do keep some Fusion cartridges and a handle around in case I don't have the time to use my vintage razor, which is more fun. I'll be tossing out the old Fusion handle in favor of the FlexBall and will probably end up using it more. Especially for special occasions where I want tobe really smooth.
